import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'
import { createSupabaseClient } from '@/lib/supabase'

export const runtime = 'nodejs'
export const dynamic = 'force-dynamic'

export async function PATCH(
  request: NextRequest,
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }
) {
  try {
    const supabase = createSupabaseClient()
    const resolvedParams = await params
    const orderId = resolvedParams.id

    // Headers anti-cache
    const headers = {
      'Cache-Control': 'no-store, no-cache, must-revalidate, max-age=0',
      'Pragma': 'no-cache',
      'Expires': '0'
    }

    const body = await request.json()
    const { status } = body

    if (!orderId) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { success: false, error: 'ID de pedido requerido' },
        { status: 400, headers }
      )
    }

    if (!status || !['pending', 'confirmed', 'prepared', 'delivered', 'cancelled'].includes(status)) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { success: false, error: 'Estado de pedido inv√°lido' },
        { status: 400, headers }
      )
    }

    console.log('üîÑ Backoffice API - Updating order status:', {
      orderId,
      newStatus: status,
      timestamp: new Date().toISOString(),
      hasServiceKey: !!process.env.SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY,
      supabaseUrl: process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL?.slice(0, 30) + '...'
    })

    // Verificar que el pedido existe
    const { data: existingOrder, error: fetchError } = await supabase
      .from('orders')
      .select('id, status')
      .eq('id', orderId)
      .single()

    if (fetchError || !existingOrder) {
      console.error('‚ùå Order not found:', fetchError)
      return NextResponse.json(
        { success: false, error: 'Pedido no encontrado' },
        { status: 404, headers }
      )
    }

    // Preparar los datos de actualizaci√≥n
    const updateData: any = {
      status,
      updated_at: new Date().toISOString()
    }

    // A√±adir timestamp espec√≠fico seg√∫n el estado
    switch (status) {
      case 'cancelled':
        updateData.cancelled_at = new Date().toISOString()
        // Nota: El trigger de cancelaci√≥n deber√≠a reponer el stock autom√°ticamente
        break
      // Los estados confirmed, prepared, delivered no tienen timestamps espec√≠ficos en el schema actual
      // Se usa updated_at para todos
    }

    // Actualizar el pedido
    const { data: updatedOrder, error: updateError } = await supabase
      .from('orders')
      .update(updateData)
      .eq('id', orderId)
      .select('*')
      .single()

    if (updateError) {
      console.error('‚ùå Update error:', updateError)
      console.error('‚ùå Update error details:', {
        message: updateError.message,
        details: updateError.details,
        hint: updateError.hint,
        code: updateError.code
      })
      return NextResponse.json(
        { success: false, error: 'Error al actualizar el pedido' },
        { status: 500, headers }
      )
    }

    console.log('‚úÖ Order status updated successfully:', {
      orderId,
      oldStatus: existingOrder.status,
      newStatus: status,
      actualUpdatedData: updatedOrder
    })

    // VERIFICACI√ìN INMEDIATA: Comprobar si el update realmente se persisti√≥
    const { data: verifyOrder, error: verifyError } = await supabase
      .from('orders')
      .select('id, status, updated_at')
      .eq('id', orderId)
      .single()

    console.log('üîç IMMEDIATE VERIFICATION after update:', {
      orderId,
      expectedStatus: status,
      actualStatus: verifyOrder?.status,
      actualUpdated: verifyOrder?.updated_at,
      verifyError: verifyError?.message,
      updateWasSuccessful: !updateError,
      verificationMatches: verifyOrder?.status === status
    })

    if (verifyOrder?.status !== status) {
      console.error('üö® CRITICAL: Update appeared successful but verification failed!')
      console.error('üö® This indicates RLS policies or transaction rollback issues')
    }

    console.log('‚úÖ Order status update completed successfully')

    return NextResponse.json({
      success: true,
      data: {
        order_id: orderId,
        old_status: existingOrder.status,
        new_status: status,
        updated_at: updateData.updated_at
      }
    }, { headers })

  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Backoffice Order Status Update API Error:', error)
    const headers = {
      'Cache-Control': 'no-store, no-cache, must-revalidate, max-age=0',
      'Pragma': 'no-cache',
      'Expires': '0'
    }
    return NextResponse.json(
      { success: false, error: 'Error interno del servidor' },
      { status: 500, headers }
    )
  }
}

Based on the search results, here's comprehensive information about excluding API routes in Next.js middleware matcher patterns in 2024:

## Excluding API Routes Using Negative Lookahead

The matcher config allows full regex, including negative lookaheads to match all except specific paths. The most common pattern for excluding API routes is:

```typescript
export const config = {
  matcher: [
    '/((?!api|_next/static|_next/image|favicon.ico).*)',
  ],
}
```

This is a negative lookahead regex that excludes paths starting with /api, /login, and Next.js internal paths.

## Alternative Pattern Examples

Another variation uses: `matcher: ["/", "/((?!studio|api).{1,})"]` to not match any route with studio or api in it.

For more specific exclusions, you can add multiple paths:

```typescript
export const config = {
  matcher: [
    '/((?!api|login|_next/static|_next/image).*)',
  ],
}
```

## Using Conditional Logic Instead

If you cannot do this with matcher because it only accepts simple path patterns, you'll need to use conditional statement:

```typescript
export function middleware(request: NextRequest) {
  if (request.nextUrl.pathname.startsWith('/api/')) {
    return NextResponse.next()
  }
  // your middleware logic
}
```

The matcher values need to be constants so they can be statically analyzed at build-time.

Both approaches are valid in 2024, with the matcher pattern being more declarative and the conditional logic providing more flexibility for complex scenarios.

Based on the search results, I found relevant information about Next.js 14 and the App Router with PATCH dynamic routes and the params Promise issue. Here's what I discovered:

## Key Issue: `params` is now a Promise in Next.js 15 (and changes from Next.js 14)

The `params` prop is a promise, and you must use async/await or React's use function to access the values.(no content)In version 14 and earlier, params was a synchronous prop.

### For Route Handlers (including PATCH)

When working with PATCH requests in dynamic routes, the proper syntax is:

The params is a promise that resolves to an object containing the dynamic route parameters for the current route, and you need to await it like: `export async function GET(request: Request, { params }: { params: Promise<{ slug: string }> }) { const { slug } = await params }`

### Common Issues Found

1. **Type Errors**: Users reported "Type error: Type 'YourPagePropsInterface' does not satisfy the constraint 'PageProps'. Types of property 'params' are incompatible. Type '{ slug: string; }' is missing the following properties from type 'Promise<any>': then, catch, finally"

2. **Solution for Next.js 14/15**: In Next.js 15 params is a promise and you have to await it, and you also have to be specific when destructuring your params

### Proper Implementation for PATCH Route Handler

```typescript
export async function PATCH(
  request: Request,
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }
) {
  const { id } = await params;
  // Your PATCH logic here
}
```

This pattern applies to all HTTP methods (GET, POST, PATCH, PUT, DELETE) in Next.js App Router route handlers with dynamic segments.
